Theater News 258

Meiyan Xia Premieres at the Central Theater with Additional Air Dance Performance: The Shanghai Film Company announced that its latest production, Meiyan Xia, directed by Du Yu and starring Yin Mingzhu, Tang Tianxiu, and Dan Erchun, premiered at the Central Theater yesterday. It is a martial arts film with a new look. The knight is a woman who subdues villains entirely with her charming eyes. The whole film is filled with a novel and beautiful atmosphere in a tense atmosphere, and it also contains humorous elements everywhere. The scenery and lighting are also very particular. There are three shows day and night, with the addition of air dance performance, whose performance is purely based on surprise and victory, such as standing people on shoulders, hanging people on kidneys, people on top of heads, kicking people on the soles of feet, using the belly as a large circle chair, and using the belly legs as thick bars, etc. It is extremely beautiful, extremely dangerous, and an unprecedented film amusement.

The Paris Theater Premieres The True and False Actresses Today: The Paris Theater announced that The True and False Actresses is a hilarious and erotic film. The trend of its humor is like the true and false uncles in our country's new drama, and like the identical brothers in Shakespeare's plays. The description of the erotic aspect is mainly based on the display of the human body beauty of models on the stage. There are three models on the stage, and one can appreciate the beauty of curves without being offensive. The theater will show it for three consecutive days starting today.

The Plum Blossom Troupe's Seven Emotions Scheduled Performance: The Plum Blossom Girls' Dance Troupe announced that the troupe's great erotic dance drama Seven Emotions, namely Pan Si Dong, has been rehearsed to perfection, and the scenery and costumes are also ready. It will be performed at the Nanjing Road City Hall for two days starting on April 4.

Social News

Urban Sketches by Lin 259

(7) A Trip Along the Suzhou Creek

In Shanghai's waterways, besides the Huangpu River, the next most important is Suzhou Creek. There are many docks along the river, and passengers traveling to Shanghai from the Suzhou-Changzhou inland river areas usually disembark at docks like Tianhougong Bridge and Pentanglong Bridge on small steamers or sailboats. Every morning around eight or nine o'clock, before the small steamers depart, the docks are crowded with people of all ages, both men and women. Soon, the whistle blows a few times, and smoky black fumes rise straight from the smokestack onto the shore. The small steamers gradually leave the riverbank and head west, pulling seven or eight boats of various sizes behind them, connected end to end, like a long snake winding along. This is a common sight on Suzhou Creek. When we read in the newspaper about lake bandits robbing small steamers, we cannot help but recall the impression we got along the shores of Suzhou Creek.

Compared to the Huangpu River, Suzhou Creek is naturally far inferior. The Huangpu River is like a large courtyard, with open gates and doors, pleasing to the eye. Suzhou Creek is not like that; it is like a narrow lane behind a stove shed, not only cramped but also carrying a dirty air. Therefore, along the Huangpu River, there are many people strolling with their hands behind their backs, gazing at the river view. The situation along the Suzhou Creek is very different. The stretch between Waibaidu Bridge and Tianhougong Bridge still has some places where one can linger and appreciate, but the further west you go, the more different it becomes. When you reach areas like Tanziwan and Xiaoshadu, it is as if you have left the city, and a desolate, bleak atmosphere permeates both banks, especially the Guangzhao Villa area, where there are few people and ghost lands are neighbors.

The scenery on both sides of the river can be divided into three distinct periods. If we use the bridges spanning the river as a standard, the section west of Waibaidu Bridge and east of Tianhougong Bridge is like a young man, with a lively and cheerful appearance. The architectural scenery on both banks exudes an air of neatness and splendor. The section between Tianhougong Bridge and the Sanban Chang Bridge at the end of Ma Gen Road is the most complex and lively. There are also the most ships on the river. This kind of tiring and endless situation is like a person in middle age, desperately trying to solve their living problems. As for the Sanban Chang Bridge, it is the last bridge on both sides of the Suzhou Creek. West of this, there are no more bridges. You have to use ferries to cross the river. The scenery on both sides becomes more desolate, as if an old man's interest in life is diminishing. In areas like Tanziwan and Xiaoshadu, many people from Jiangbei live on small boats, but these boats never float on the water; they are beached and live close to the shore. These lifeless boats can well represent the general situation of this section of the Suzhou Creek.

The first section of the Suzhou Creek includes Waibaidu Bridge, Libaidu Bridge, Sichuan Road Bridge, Jiangxi Road Bridge, and Tianhougong Bridge (Henan Road Bridge). The "Bai" character in "Waibaidu Bridge" is probably a corruption of the character "摆". That place also has a name called "Tou Ba". These two words can tell us a little about what the Suzhou Creek was like decades ago. Standing on the bridge and looking east, the water of the Huangpu River flows right under your feet into Suzhou Creek. To the south is the Bund Park, a piece of land forming the enclosure at the intersection of the two rivers. The Western name of Waibaidu Bridge is "Garden Bridge". Bund Park is indeed very relevant. At the base of the bridge, there is indeed a garden dedicated to growing flowers. Standing on the bridge, you can have a panoramic view of it. Among them, a glass flower house is extraordinarily quiet. Against the wall is a natural spring, with water flowing from above into the pool, and green shadows reflected on it, further highlighting the tranquility of the room.

Looking west from the bridge, the nearest is the Erbaidu Bridge. The two banks of the Erbaidu Bridge are also decorated with "leisurely" elements. On the south side, along the river bank, there are often yachts burning gasoline, moored on the river. The inside of the boat is cleaned as clean as a hospital. The old boatmen also reveal a self-respecting attitude. Apart from accompanying their masters on outings, they spend the day cleaning and wiping the boat, so dirt and dust are completely foreign to them. Among the boats entering and exiting Suzhou Creek, some carry passengers, and some tow goods. Nine out of ten boats are bloated. Only the yachts are slender, with well-proportioned bones and flesh, like the young ladies of Suzhou Creek.

Between the Baidu Bridge and the Sichuan Road Bridge, there are churches, hospitals, hotels, movie theaters, and garden shops along the banks. Especially near the Libaidu Bridge on the south bank, the roads are flat, and the scenery is quiet and serene. When the sun is setting, the river breeze blows from the east, stroking people's faces, no less than a walk along the river. The post office at the northern end of the Sichuan Road Bridge is the only important building along the Suzhou Creek. The Commerce Association at Tianhougong Bridge also has its own place. When Tianhougong was reorganized, there were many stalls and astrologers inside. There were also many people who worshipped the gods. Besides the City God Temple and the Red Temple, Tianhougong could be considered the third in line. Now, the front is deserted, not as good as before. This is also a change related to the Suzhou Creek.

Looking at the traffic and pedestrians coming and going from the bridge is almost a unique scenery of the Suzhou Creek. There is an iron frame on the Waibaidu Bridge, crisscrossing and arching high above the bridge. At night, when a streetcar passes over the bridge, looking from afar, the lights from the carriages shine through the gaps, which is very interesting. At night, along the Suzhou Creek, you can also see the spires of the three department stores, towering high in the sky. Looking back east, although there are tall things behind, the lights on the boat are reflected in the water, rippling and swaying. The air on both banks seems to be much quieter, but a motorcycle quickly drives over the bridge, and the quiet air vibrates like the river water.

The Eunuch Sanbao in the Southern Seas YS 260

(10) Sanbao Cave

This was the seventh voyage of Eunuch Sanbao, and also his last trip to the Southern Seas. It was the year 1433. He, along with over twenty thousand soldiers and civilians, sailed in dozens of "Big Eye Chicken" ships towards the Southern Seas.

Once, as these dozens of "Big Eye Chicken" ships were sailing smoothly along, for some reason, a monstrous wave suddenly arose, and the wind began to howl. These dozens of "Big Eye Chicken" ships drifted like cradles in the vast ocean, tossed about by the waves.

At this time, all the soldiers and civilians on those dozens of "Big Eye Chicken" ships were vomiting. They vomited severely, and naturally, they had no strength left. At this point, the capable Eunuch Sanbao could not think of any remedy. This group of pitiful vomiting soldiers and civilians could only lie down in the cradle-like "Big Eye Chicken" ships, "resigned to their fate."

Soon, the waves grew increasingly larger, and the wind became increasingly fierce. At this point, the ships rocked even more violently. The mountain-toppling, sea-overturning rocking only made that group of vomiting soldiers and civilians feel even more intensely miserable.

Even Eunuch Sanbao began to vomit at this time. He could not think of any solution. The thought of "resigning to fate" might have floated into his mind at this point. Therefore, besides lying down, he seemed to be indifferent to everything, as if nothing mattered to him anymore.

The wind and waves grew larger day by day. This was already the third day, and the waves still showed no sign of calming down.

The wind and waves on the fourth day were even more ferocious. These dozens of "Big Eye Chicken" ships, which had originally been sailing together, had already been scattered by the wind and waves. However, those pitiful soldiers and civilians lying in the "Big Eye Chicken" ships were still completely unaware.

On the fifth day, Eunuch Sanbao could no longer endure this suffering, so he began to curse.

"If I still have to suffer such great wind and waves, I would rather die and be done with it!" As soon as he finished speaking, a huge wave overturned his solitary ship. Consequently, the people on board were completely drowned, and the ship slowly sank to the bottom of the sea, it is said.

The day after Eunuch Sanbao's ship sank, the wind and waves actually stopped. Who knew that not far from the location where Eunuch Sanbao's ship sank, there were small, desolate islands?

Time passed like lightning. A month quickly passed. At this time, in a remote part of that desolate island, a cave emerged. That cave, viewed from a distance, looked just like an overturned ship. The cave was overgrown with many strange trees, and those trees hung down like iron chains in a tangled mess. As for this cave, it is said to be Eunuch Sanbao's ship. Later, for some reason, this legend of Sanbao Cave spread among the people in the south.
